            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  In response to the change of energy landscape, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are becoming one of the most promising power sources for the post-lithium-ion battery (LIB) era due to the cheap and abundant nature of sodium, and similar electrochem. properties to LIBs.  The electrochem. performance of electrode materials for SIBs is closely bound up with their crystal structures and intrinsic electronic/ionic states.  Apart from nanoscale design and conductive composite strategies, heteroatom doping is another effective way to enhance the intrinsic transfer characteristics of sodium ions and electrons in crystal structures to accelerate reaction kinetics and thereby achieve high performance.  In this review, the recent advancements in heteroatom doping for sodium ion storage of electrode materials are reviewed.  Specifically, different doping strategies including nonmetal element doping (e.g., nitrogen, sulfur, phosphorous, boron, fluorine), metal element doping (magnesium, titanium, iron, aluminum, nickel, copper, etc.), and dual/triple doping (such as N-S, N-P, N-S-P) are reviewed and summarized in detail.  Furthermore, various doping methods are introduced and their advantages and disadvantages are discussed.  The doping effect on crystal structure and intrinsic electronic/ionic state are illustrated and the relationship with capacity and energy/power d. is interrogated.  Finally, future development trends in doping strategies for advanced SIBs electrodes are analyzed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoca4zmQM8fj7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgLtmGlG1gADw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtVyrsb7N&amp;md5=178aa553953d90a51a9b53b47bd04654</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2020.12.010"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">PVP-assisted Synthesis of g-C<sub>3</sub>N<sub>4</sub>-derived N-doped Graphene with Tunable Interplanar Spacing as High-performance Lithium/sodium Ions Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>174</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">98</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">109</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">PVP-assisted synthesis of g-C3N4-derived N-doped graphene with tunable interplanar spacing as high-performance lithium/sodium ions battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tang, Yihua; Wang, Xiao; Chen, Jingjing; Wang, Xinxin; Wang, Dajian; Mao, Zhiyong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">174</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">98-109</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon materials have attracted abundant attentions and been utilized widely as anodes in rechargeable Li+/Na+/K+ ions batteries.  Regarding the various radius of alkali-metal-ions, reversible intercalation and deintercalation in interlayers of carbons requires different interplanar spacing.  In this work, N-doped graphene with tunable interplanar spacing is synthesized using graphitic carbon nitride (g-C3N4) as precursor with the assistance of polyvinylpyrrolidone (PVP).  The obtained tunable interplanar spacing in the range from 0.34-0.45 nm with enlarged values is mainly ascribed to the high nitrogen doping levels (9.98-33.7 at. %), esp. to the pyrrolic nitrogen.  Serving as the anode materials in lithium ions batteries (LIBs) and sodium ions batteries (SIBs), promising specific capacities of 1236 mAh g-1 for LIBs and 300 mAh g-1 for SIBs at c.d. of 0.05 A g-1 and excellent cycling stability as well as acceptable rate capability are demonstrated for the resultant N-doped graphene.  The effect of interplanar spacing on the electrochem. performances of LIBs and SIBs are investigated comparatively.  This work outlines a facial route to synthesize N-doped graphene with tunable interplanar spacing, meeting the various requirements unitized as anodes in rechargeable Li+/Na+/K+ ions batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrS4Gw3IeSu67Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgLtmGlG1gADw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Superior Oxygen Reduction Reaction on Phosphorus-Doped Carbon Dot/Graphene Aerogel for All-Solid-State Flexible Al-Air Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Mengran; Li, Yuan; Fang, Jing; Villa, Cesar J.; Xu, Yaobin; Hao, Shiqiang; Li, Jie; Liu, Yexiang; Wolverton, Chris; Chen, Xinqi; Dravid, Vinayak P.; Lai, Yanqing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1902736</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon dots have been recognized as one of the most promising candidates for the oxygen redn. reaction (ORR) in alk. media.  However, the desired ORR performance in metal-air batteries is often limited by the moderate electrocatalytic activity and the lack of a method to realize good dispersion.  To address these issues, herein a biomass-deriving method is reported to achieve the in situ phosphorus doping (P-doping) of carbon dots and their simultaneous decoration onto graphene matrix.  The resultant product, namely P-doped carbon dot/graphene (P-CD/G) nanocomposites, can reach an ultrahigh P-doping level for carbon nanomaterials.  The P-CD/G nanocomposites are found to exhibit excellent ORR activity, which is highly comparable to the com. Pt/C catalysts.  When used as the cathode materials for a primary liq. Al-air battery, the device shows an impressive power d. of 157.3 mW cm-2 (comparing to 151.5 mW cm-2 of a similar Pt/C battery).  Finally, an all-solid-state flexible Al-air battery is designed and fabricated based on our new nanocomposites.  The device exhibits a stable discharge voltage of ≈1.2 V upon different bending states.  This study introduces a unique biomass-derived material system to replace the noble metal catalysts for future portable and wearable electronic devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqWiV_-P6zS_bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgLtmGlG1gADw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">"Protrusions" or "holes" in graphene: which is the better choice for sodium ion storage?</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Yijun; Tang, Dai-Ming; Zhang, Chao; Zhang, Yihui; Liang, Qifeng; Chen, Shimou; Weng, Qunhong; Zhou, Min; Xue, Yanming; Liu, Jiangwei; Wu, Jinghua; Cui, Qiu Hong; Lian, Chao; Hou, Guolin; Yuan, Fangli; Bando, Yoshio; Golberg, Dmitri; Wang, Xi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">979-986</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The main challenge assocd. with sodium-ion battery (SIB) anodes is a search for novel candidate materials with high capacity and excellent rate capability.  The most commonly used and effective route for graphene-based anode design is the introduction of in-plane "hole" defects via nitrogen-doping; this creates a spacious reservoir for storing more energy.  Inspired by mountains in nature, herein, we propose another way - the introduction of blistering in graphene instead of making "holes"; this facilitates adsorbing/inserting more Na+ ions.  In order to properly answer the key question: ""protrusions" or "holes" in graphene, which is better for sodium ion storage", two types of anode materials with a similar doping level were designed: a phosphorus-doped graphene (GP, with protrusions) and a nitrogen-doped graphene (GN, with holes).  As compared with GN, the GP anode perfectly satisfies all the desired criteria: it reveals an ultrahigh capacity (374 mA h g-1 after 120 cycles at 25 mA g-1) comparable to the best graphite anodes in a std. Li-ion battery (∼372 mA h g-1), and exhibits an excellent rate capability (210 mA h g-1 at 500 mA g-1).  In situ transmission electron microscopy (TEM) expts. and d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. were utilized to uncover the origin of the enhanced electrochem. activity of "protrusions" compared to "holes" in SIBs, down to the at. scale.  The introduction of protrusions through P-doping into graphene is envisaged to be a novel effective way to enhance the capacity and rate performance of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrZF4LZN3ZV3LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgLtmGlG1gADw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Integrated N, P co-doped and dense carbon networks produced by a chemical crosslinking strategy: Facilitating high gravimetric/volumetric performance sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Haijun; Yuan, Haocheng; Zhan, Wenwei; Lee, Young-Seak; Shin, Hee-Jae; Wei, Xianbin; Cai, Qing; Lan, Jin-Le; Yu, Yunhua; Yang, Xiaoping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">165</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Low-cost sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have shown hopeful perspective for large-scale energy storage systems.  However, the development of carbon anode materials with high gravimetric and volumetric capacity is still a challenge.  Herein, we propose a novel dense and N, P co-doped carbon derived from high d. crosslinked bacterial cellulose (BC) with hexachlorocyclotriphosphazene (HCCP), which simultaneously combines high gravimetric and volumetric capacity.  The as-prepd. electrode demonstrates a high reversible capacity of 223 mAh g-1 at 0.05 A g-1 and superior rate performance (145 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1) based on the overall electrode materials.  The full SIBs with this electrode show a high energy d. (156.1 Wh kg-1) as well as a high Coulombic efficiency in the potential range of 0-4.2 V.  D. functional theory (DFT) calcn. and kinetic anal. reveals that the synergistic effect of N, P co-doped configurations contributes to the superior sodium storage performance.  Moreover, this electrode possesses high pressing d. of 1.40 g cm-3, which increases the volumetric capacity greatly (from 97.2 to 312.2 mAh cm-3).  This work proposes a new idea towards the development of low-cost bacterial cellulose that can be used in practical applications for high gravimetric and volumetric performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp2aPMIsc74nrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrioitZbrbrw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXoslejtr8%253D&amp;md5=b36ca0d77510ec6dac9938b3e4792155</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1016/j.jmst.2020.11.014"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Experimental Design and Theoretical Evaluation of Nitrogen and Phosphorus Dual-doped Hierarchical Porous Carbon for High-performance Sodium-ion Storage</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Experimental design and theoretical evaluation of nitrogen and phosphorus dual-doped hierarchical porous carbon for high-performance sodium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Chen; Huang, Ying; Meng, Zhuoyue; Lu, Mengwei; Xu, Zhipeng; Liu, Panbo; Li, Tiehu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Science &amp; Technology (Shenyang, China)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">76</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11-19</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JSCTEQ</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Editorial Board of Journal of Materials Science &amp; Technology</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Starch has a wide range of sources and can be used as a high-quality precursor for sodium-ion battery anode materials.  However, the carbonization yield and specific capacity of carbon materials obtained by directly pyrolyzing starch are low.  Herein, starch is used as the carbon source, and ammonium polyphosphate (APP) is used as the crosslinking agent and dopant to prep. a nitrogen and phosphorus co-doped porous carbon (NPPC).  As the anode for sodium-ion batteries, NPPC-2 exhibits a high reversible capacity of 385.8 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1.  Even after 1000 cycles at a large c.d. of 5 A g-1, the reversible capacity can still be maintained at 126.9 mA h g-1.  Based on detailed data and first-principles calcns., the excellent performance of NPPC is due to the effective doping of nitrogen and phosphorus elements, which distorts the graphite sheet, introduces defects, and increases the graphite layer spacing, thereby enhancing the adsorption capacity of the carbon material for sodium ions, reducing the diffusion barrier of sodium ions.  This work provides a new idea for heteroatom doping and carbon material modification.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGplKgqpTESGPrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrioitZbrbrw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhtFehtrfL&amp;md5=2dae9702ee3c3f14be2adaf188438a76</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1016/j.apsusc.2020.146221"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Chemical Grafting-Derived N, P Co-doped Hollow Microporous Carbon Spheres for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Appl. Surf. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>518</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">146221</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.apsusc.2020.146221</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D518%26publication_year%3D2020%26journal%3DAppl.%2BSurf.%2BSci.%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BLan%26author%3DH.%2BYuan%26author%3DS.%2BLuo%26author%3DY.%2BHuang%26author%3DY.%2BYu%26author%3DQ.%2BCai%26author%3DX.%2BYang%26title%3DChemical%2BGrafting-Derived%2BN%252C%2BP%2BCo-doped%2BHollow%2BMicroporous%2BCarbon%2BSpheres%2Bfor%2BHigh-Performance%2BSodium-Ion%2BBattery%2BAnodes%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.apsusc.2020.146221&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.2c17789&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.apsusc.2020.146221&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Chemical Grafting-derived N, P co-doped Hollow Microporous Carbon Spheres for High-Performance Sodium-ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Haijun; Lan, Jin-Le; Yuan, Haocheng; Luo, Shicheng; Huang, Yiqian; Yu, Yunhua; Cai, Qing; Yang, Xiaoping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Surface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">518</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">146221</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ASUSEE</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0169-4332</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Microstructure design combined with high-level heteroatoms doping has been considered the leading approach for prepg. the high-performance carbon anodes for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, a hollow porous carbon sphere (NP-HPCS) that exhibits a high N, P co-doping level (6.05 at% for N, 5.19 at% for P) and a large microporous specific area (339 m2 g-1) is reported.  The microporous and N, P co-doping synergistic construction of the NP-HPCS was achieved by a high-efficiency chem. grafting of hexachlorocyclotriphosphazene (HCCP) onto polydopamine (PDA) shell, accompanied by the in situ micellar transformation of pore-forming agent F127 in the grafting process.  The as-prepd. NP-HPCS used as an anode for SIBs delivers a superior rate capacity (∼101 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1) and an excellent long cycle performance (∼120 mAh g-1 after 5000 cycles at 5 A g-1).  The kinetics anal. and d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. were carried out to further analyze the superior sodium storage performance of NP-HPCS.  The work suggests an effective way to develop high-performance carbon anode materials for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoKxeDfGe8jOrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrioitZbrbrw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXmtlCjurw%253D&amp;md5=fd58ea208f6b0b0a559eb094b01bb7a6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA04169D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Panja, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bhattacharjya, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nitrogen and Phosphorus Co-doped Cubic Ordered Mesoporous Carbon as a Supercapacitor Electrode Material with Extraordinary Cyclic Stability</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">18001</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">18009</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C5TA04169D</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D18001-18009%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DT.%2BPanja%26author%3DD.%2BBhattacharjya%26author%3DJ.%2BYu%26title%3DNitrogen%2Band%2BPhosphorus%2BCo-doped%2BCubic%2BOrdered%2BMesoporous%2BCarbon%2Bas%2Ba%2BSupercapacitor%2BElectrode%2BMaterial%2Bwith%2BExtraordinary%2BCyclic%2BStability%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC5TA04169D&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.2c17789&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC5TA04169D&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen and phosphorus co-doped cubic ordered mesoporous carbon as a supercapacitor electrode material with extraordinary cyclic stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Panja, Tandra; Bhattacharjya, Dhrubajyoti; Yu, Jong-Sung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">35</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18001-18009</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Heteroatoms and porosity both have different, but definite effects on the electrochem. capacitance of C materials.  These effects are studied in detail by using cubic ordered mesoporous carbons (OMCs) co-doped with N and P. 3-Dimensional (3D) mesoporous SiO2, KIT-6, with bicontinuous cubic Ia3d symmetry is used as a hard template to synthesize the cubic OMCs.  Although the porosity parameters e.g. surface area and pore vol. do not change much with N doping, a significant increase of these values is obsd. upon P doping.  Also, the P content does not affect the N doping characteristics on co-doping of both N and P.  When tested as a supercapacitor electrode, the N-OMC, despite its much lower porosity parameters, exhibits a similar specific capacitance to that of the P-OMC.  The high specific capacitance of N-OMC arises mainly from the pseudocapacitive effect of doped N species, whereas high porosity parameters are the main reason for the specific capacitance shown by P-OMC.  The synergistic contribution of both effects enables the NP co-doped OMC to show the highest specific capacitance of 210 F g-1 at 1.0 A g-1.  Also, excellent retention of specific capacitance with &gt;90% of initial capacitance is obsd. for NP-OMC at a high c.d. of 10 A g-1 and also for 3000 charge-discharge cycles.  This is mainly because of high-surface area hierarchical porous structures with uniform and ordered mesopores in the cubic OMC, which facilitate the unrestricted movement of electrolyte ions to access the active surfaces, as well as the excellent synergistic effect of co-doping of N and P.  This is also supported by electrochem. impedance spectroscopic anal., which shows negligible mass transfer resistance and internal cell resistance.  Overall, the synthesized cubic OMC materials are highly promising as electrodes for supercapacitors and other energy-related applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmFegT-urn7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrioitZbrbrw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXht1ajurvJ&amp;md5=c54602ceee540c571b37302a19103687</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1039/C9TA08151H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xi, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Three-dimensional Nitrogen and Phosphorus Co-doped carbon Quantum Dots/reduced Graphene Oxide Composite Aerogels with a Hierarchical Porous Structure as Superior Electrode Materials for Supercapacitors</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-dimensional nitrogen and phosphorus co-doped carbon quantum dots/reduced graphene oxide composite aerogels with a hierarchical porous structure as superior electrode materials for supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Jingying; Yun, Xiaoru; Hu, Zhongliang; Xi, Liujiang; Li, Na; Tang, Heng; Lu, Pengcheng; Zhu, Yirong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">46</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">26311-26325</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">C quantum dot (CQD)-based electrode materials as a novel kind of emerging materials have recently received increasing interest owing to their many unique properties.  Here, graphitic CQDs are synthesized by a modified chem. oxidn. approach, and further utilized as the intercalator to prep. novel 3-dimensional (3D) N, P co-doped CQDs/reduced graphene oxide (rGO) composite aerogels (N, P-CQDs/rGO) by a 1-step hydrothermal approach.  When used as an electrode material for supercapacitors for the 1st time, the as-obtained N, P-CQDs/rGO exhibits a notably enhanced specific capacitance (453.7 F/g at 1 A/g) compared with GO, rGO, N, P-rGO and CQDs/rGO.  The as-synthesized N, P-CQDs/rGO presents excellent rate properties (69.5% of capacitance retention at 50 A/g) and cycle performance (93.5% of capacity retention at 10 A/g over 10,000 cycles).  The good capacitive behaviors can be ascribed to the synergistic effect of N, P co-doping modification, the introduction of CQDs and the unique 3D porous aerogel structure with a large sp. surface area, hierarchical porous structure and superior elec. cond.  A sym. device is assembled based on the N, P-CQDs/rGO composite aerogel, achieving a high energy d. of 15.69 Wh/Kg at a power d. of 325 W/Kg, and superior cycle stability with 85.5% of capacitance retention at 5 A/g over 10,000 cycles.  This current work can offer a promising strategy for the design and development of novel and high-performance 3D CQD-based composite aerogels for application in supercapacitors and other energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoeQGsRTN9hnbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwHetfiiQyig"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly efficient nitrogen-doped carbide-derived carbon materials for oxygen reduction reaction in alkaline media</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ratso, Sander; Kruusenberg, Ivar; Kaarik, Maike; Kook, Mati; Saar, Rando; Pars, Martti; Leis, Jaan; Tammeveski, Kaido</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, a novel type of nitrogen-doped carbide-derived carbon (N-CDC) catalysts is synthesized and their activity toward the oxygen redn. reaction (ORR) is investigated.  Two different methods of prepn. of N-CDC materials are compared: chlorination of titanium carbonitride and pyrolysis in the presence of a nitrogen-contg. compd. (dicyandiamide) of pre-chlorinated titanium carbide.  The obtained catalysts are tested for ORR activity in 0.1 M KOH soln. using the rotating disk electrode method along with their stability during 1000 cycles and compared to a com. Pt/C catalyst.  The surface morphol. is investigated using SEM and the bulk compn. with energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy.  The surface compn. of the catalyst materials is analyzed with XPS and the structure with X-ray diffraction and Raman spectroscopy.  The porosity of N-CDC materials is described with N2 physisorption.  The dicyandiamide-derived N-doped CDC material showed excellent electrocatalytic activity for ORR in alk. media.  This N-CDC catalyst could be considered as a promising cathode material in alk. fuel cells.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoIpdYLTjtac7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwHetfiiQyig"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhvFGjsbzO&amp;md5=b8f80cb8e9471598ca23bc2ca5471b23</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemrev.0c00080"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mei, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Matyjaszewski, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Antonietti, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polymer-Derived Heteroatom-Doped Porous Carbon Materials</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polymer-Derived Heteroatom-Doped Porous Carbon Materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Hong; Shao, Yue; Mei, Shilin; Lu, Yan; Zhang, Miao; Sun, Jian-ke; Matyjaszewski, Krzysztof; Antonietti, Markus; Yuan, Jiayin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Reviews (Washington, DC, United States)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">120</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9363-9419</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHREAY</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Heteroatom-doped porous carbon materials (HPCMs) have found extensive applications in adsorption/sepn., org. catalysis, sensing, and energy conversion/storage.  The judicious choice of carbon precursors is crucial for the manuf. of HPCMs with specific usages and maximization of their functions.  In this regard, polymers as precursors have demonstrated great promise because of their versatile mol. and nanoscale structures, modulatable chem. compn., and rich processing techniques to generate textures that, in combination with proper solid-state chem., can be maintained throughout carbonization.  This Review comprehensively surveys the progress in polymer-derived functional HPCMs in terms of how to produce and control their porosities, heteroatom doping effects, and morphologies and their related use.  First, we summarize and discuss synthetic approaches, including hard and soft templating methods as well as direct synthesis strategies employing polymers to control the pores and/or heteroatoms in HPCMs.  Second, we summarize the heteroatom doping effects on the thermal stability, electronic and optical properties, and surface chem. of HPCMs.  Specifically, the heteroatom doping effect, which involves both single-type heteroatom doping and codoping of two or more types of heteroatoms into the carbon network, is discussed.  Considering the significance of the morphologies of HPCMs in their application spectrum, potential choices of suitable polymeric precursors and strategies to precisely regulate the morphologies of HPCMs are presented.  Finally, we provide our perspective on how to predefine the structures of HPCMs by using polymers to realize their potential applications in the current fields of energy generation/conversion and environmental remediation.  We believe that these analyses and deductions are valuable for a systematic understanding of polymer-derived carbon materials and will serve as a source of inspiration for the design of future HPCMs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoPdxYEZ2ZYL7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwHetfiiQyig"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsFahu7bF&amp;md5=3369bd71795e4c4687da52bf9492ea92</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2020.07.021"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, D.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, O.                 10.1016/j.carbon.2020.07.021</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D168%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D448-457%26journal%3DCarbon%26author%3DD.-Y.%2BKim%26author%3DO.%2BL.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BKang%26title%3DNovel%2BSynthesis%2Bof%2BHighly%2BPhosphorus-doped%2BCarbon%2Bas%2Ban%2BUltrahigh-Rate%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.carbon.2020.07.021&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.2c17789&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.carbon.2020.07.021&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Novel synthesis of highly phosphorus-doped carbon as an ultrahigh-rate anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Dae-Yeong; Li, Oi Lun; Kang, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">168</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">448-457</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbonaceous materials are the most promising anode materials in electrochem. energy storage systems.  However, poor electrochem. performance is a major obstacle to their practical use.  Here, P-doped carbon balls (PCBs) are synthesized through a simple novel method, the soln. plasma process (SPP), which is different from the conventional synthesis method, and used as an anode material in sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  The PCBs synthesized by this approach show a high P content of about 4 at%.  Meanwhile, P doping and disordered amorphous structures of PCBs provide abundant active sites and capacitive-dominant Na+ adsorption behavior, while large amts. of meso- and macropores shorten the Na+ diffusion distance, accelerating ion transport.  The PCB anode material provides a high initial coulombic efficiency of about 75% and a high reversible capacity of 340 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 1 A g-1.  Even at an ultrahigh c.d. of 100 A g-1, an outstanding rate performance of 130 mA g-1 and reversible capacity of 83 mAh g-1 after 40,000 cycles provide excellent cycling stability.  This synthesis strategy not only provides a very efficient approach to heteroatom doping but will also be a great impetus for the practical use of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPPVE2NGzgkrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwHetfiiQyig"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsFegtL%252FF&amp;md5=b11f45d57f662ec6a03348b67b672d9d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.0c23165"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mizota, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Regulate Phosphorus Configuration in High P-doped Hard Carbon as a Superanode for Sodium Storage</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                 10.1021/acsami.0c23165</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D12059-12068%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DM.%2BHou%26author%3DZ.%2BShi%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26author%3DI.%2BMizota%26author%3DH.%2BLou%26author%3DB.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BHou%26title%3DRegulate%2BPhosphorus%2BConfiguration%2Bin%2BHigh%2BP-doped%2BHard%2BCarbon%2Bas%2Ba%2BSuperanode%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.0c23165&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.2c17789&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.0c23165&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Regulate Phosphorus Configuration in High P-Doped Hard Carbon as a Superanode for Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xiaoyan; Hou, Mingxing; Shi, Zhenglu; Liu, Xiang; Mizota, Isao; Lou, Hongtao; Wang, Bin; Hou, Xianhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12059-12068</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Heteroatom-doped hard carbon is a popular method to optimize the electrochem. performance of anode electrodes for sodium-ion batteries.  Herein, phosphorus-doped hollow carbon nanorods (P-HCNs) are obtained by a one-step synthesis with a high phosphorus content of 7.5 atom %.  By controlling the P configuration, the P-HCNs03 exhibits reversible capacity as high as 260 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 1.0 A g-1 after 500 cycles with an initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 73%.  When the amt. of phosphorus in the as-prepd. materials is changed, the different structures of the P-doped carbon lattices are analyzed by X-ray diffraction, Raman spectroscopy, and XPS.  Based on the first-principles calcn., although the P-O bond has the most configurations, the excellent reversible capacity of the electrode is attributed to the strong Na-absorption ability of P=O and P-C bonds.  The sodium-based dual-ion batteries (NDIBs) assembled with P-HCNs03 as an anode and expanded graphite as a cathode (P-HCNs03//EG) exhibited a high energy d. of 138 W h kg-1 at a power d. of 159 W kg-1.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phosphorus-Doped Hard Carbon Nanofibers Prepared by Electrospinning as an Anode in Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Feng; Dong, Ruiqi; Bai, Ying; Li, Yu; Chen, Guanghai; Wang, Zhaohua; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phosphorus-doped hard carbon nanofibers with macroporous structure were successfully synthesized by electrospinning followed by a thermal treatment process using polyacrylonitrile and H3PO4 as carbon and phosphorus precursors, resp.  XPS anal. reveals that the doped phosphorus atoms can incorporate into the carbon framework and most of them are connecting with carbon atoms to form P-C bond.  The (002) plane interlayer spacing was taken from the X-ray diffraction pattern, which shows a large spacing of 3.83 Å for the obtained P-doped hard carbon nanofibers.  When used as an anode in sodium-ion batteries, the as-prepd. P-doped hard carbon nanofibers can deliver a reversible capacity of 288 and 103 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 50 mA g-1 and 2 A g-1, resp.  After 200 cycles at 50 mA g-1, the capacity retention of P-doped hard carbon nanofibers still reaches 87.8%, demonstrating good cycling durability.  These excellent electrochem. performances of P-doped hard carbon nanofibers can be attributed to the macroporous structure, large interlayer spacing, and the formation of P-C bond.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpQsDJ4Qu6jkrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj9wObg328lvQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtVKgtLjN&amp;md5=f7fe4c603207e1d5f8ab260923b0fbfa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA06113J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nie, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sheng, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Porous Nitrogen and Phosphorus Co-Doped Carbon Nanofiber Networks for High Performance Electrical Double Layer Capacitors</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-standing hard carbon anode derived from hyper-linked nanocellulose with high cycling stability for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yan; Du, Yi-Feng; Sun, Guo-Hua; Cheng, Jia-Yao; Song, Ge; Song, Ming-Xin; Su, Fang-Yuan; Yang, Fan; Xie, Li-Jing; Chen, Cheng-Meng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">EcoMat</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The utilization of binders has severely hindered ionic diffusion and electron transfer in the traditional lithium-ion battery.  Herein, a self-standing hard carbon film using nanocellulose as precursor has been constructed as binder-free electrodes via two-step thermal treatment.  The cyclization and aromatization of small mol. fragments promote the formation of hyper-crosslinked framework with abundant welded junctions.  Importantly, carbon nanofibers not only serve as an inter-connected conductive network for fast electron transfer, but also as an interlinked mech. skeleton for convenient Li+ diffusion and electrode structural stability.  Furthermore, the optimized carbon film, with accessible redox-active carbonyl groups (C=O) and abundant micropores, is beneficial for Li+ accommodation.  It exhibits high reversible capacity of 513.1 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 and excellent cycle stability to extend over 1000 cycles without signs of decay.  This study provides an efficient strategy for the design of high-performance biomass-derived anode materials with stable-structure for alk. batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrTJ-OH9wWdLrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj9wObg328lvQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXptFKmur8%253D&amp;md5=f32ef8ff8e8bb84b1e4e925da241a070</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA05621D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrospun Cross-linked Carbon Nanofiber Films as Free-standing and Binder-free Anodes with Superior Rate Performance and Long-Term Cycling Stability for Sodium Ion Storage</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">21343</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">21352</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospun cross-linked carbon nanofiber films as free-standing and binder-free anodes with superior rate performance and long-term cycling stability for sodium ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Xu; Zhang, Xiaoting; Song, Huaihe; Zhou, Jisheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">21343-21352</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A crosslinking strategy is proposed to design electrospun C nanofiber films towards free-standing and binder-free electrodes with high Na-ion storage performance.  Based on this strategy, electrospun cross-linked C nanofiber (CL-CNF) films are fabricated with polyvinylpyrrolidone solns. contg. Cu(NO3)2.  The formation of the cross-linked structure should be ascribed to the strong coordination of PVP with Cu(NO3)2, which acts as a crosslinking agent.  The as-prepd. CL-CNF film is flexible, and the av. diam. of the nanofibers can be facilely adjusted by controlling the feeding rate.  Remarkably, the CL-CNF film demonstrates an excellent rate performance and long cycle stability when used as a binder-free anode for SIBs, compared with the CNF film without a cross-linked structure.  At 50 mA g-1, the CL-CNF film delivered a specific capacity of ≤449 mA h g-1, which can rival the Na ion storage capacity of most of the reported electrospun nanofibers.  At 5 and 10 A g-1, the CL-CNF film delivers an initial reversible capacity of 148 and 121 mA h g-1, resp., and still maintains 126 and 111 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles without obvious capacity fading.  The excellent electrochem. properties of the CNF film are attributed to the unique cross-linked structure that endows the CL-CNF film with fast electron transfer and ion diffusion kinetics as well as robust structural stability to bear the repeated impact of Na ions during the discharge/charge process.  Therefore, this work opens up a new strategy to design high performance C nanofibers as free-standing electrodes for flexible energy Na-ion storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqT2sOY3ubrdLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj9wObg328lvQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsVyitbjM&amp;md5=85da9f6cbe67f48ed71d10e47ab135f7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201600243"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Large-Area Carbon Nanosheets Doped with Phosphorus: A High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A sustainable route from corn stalks to N, P-dual doping carbon sheets toward high performance sodium-ion batteries anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qin, Decai; Liu, Zhanying; Zhao, Yanzhang; Xu, Guiyin; Zhang, Fang; Zhang, Xiaogang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">130</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">664-671</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High performance is indispensable for amorphous carbon materials toward sodium-ion batteries anode.  Heteroatom doping has proved to be an effective strategy to improve the electrochem. performance of carbon-based materials.  In this paper, N, P dual-doped carbon sheets (N, P-CS) from the rinds of corn stalks have been successfully synthesized via a hydrothermal reaction using the cheap (NH4)2HPO4 as nitrogen and phosphorus source.  SEM and TEM images showed that the N, P-CS was composed of loose and stacked graphitic carbon sheets, which facilitated the penetration of electrolyte and ion diffusion.  Higher ID/IG value (1.692) implied more defective sites on the surface of graphitic sheet to be generated after N and P co-doping, which combined with larger graphene layer distance (0.391 nm) contributed to the high performance of the N, P-CS.  When used as anode for sodium ion batteries, it presents a specific capacity of 277mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.25C, and a specific capacity of 202 mAh g-1 after 200 cycles at 1C.  Even at a high rate of 5C, a stable specific capacity of 105 mAh g-1 still could be delivered after 2000 cycles, suggesting an excellent cycle stability and superior rate capability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpf3SmY7mnYm7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg--IiNAF-JZQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Scalable fabrication of heteroatom-doped versatile hierarchical porous carbons with an all-in-one phthalonitrile precursor and their applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Weng, Zhihuan; Zhang, Kewen; Qi, Yu; Zhang, Tianpeng; Xia, Miao; Hu, Fangyuan; Zhang, Shouhai; Liu, Cheng; Wang, Jinyan; Jian, Xigao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">159</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">495-503</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Heteroatom-doped hierarchical porous carbons with large sp. surface area and high heteroatom content are important but they generally require multistep syntheses and harsh conditions.  A scalable and straightforward strategy is introduced to synthesize N/O co-doped hierarchical porous carbons (DNKs) derived from an all-in-one phthalonitrile precursor 1,3-bis(3,4-dicyanophenoxy)benzene (DPPH) with the assistant of potassium hydroxide and urea.  In this facile and template-free method, all the raw materials are placed in the tube furnace, and the 1-pot process involves polymn., carbonization, and activation.  At 1 bar, ultra-high CO2 uptake of 7.27 mmol/g at 273°K was achieved for the sample DNK@550, which can be attribute to its well-developed micropore structure and abundant nitrogen content (7.93 wt%).  Moreover, the distinct features of DNK@650 afforded a high specific capacitance of 487 F/g at a c.d. of 0.1 A/g in a 3-electrode system using 1 M H2SO4 aq. as electrolyte.  Most importantly, the fabricated sym. supercapacitor exhibited excellent cycling stability over a new cycle record of 100,000 (capacitor retention of ∼103%).  This work provides new insights for the fabrication of versatile porous carbons from readily available and flexible precursors via a facile and scalable route.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqp44xbtUZwGLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg--IiNAF-JZQ"> &gt;&gt; Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2970</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2977</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries Based on Nitrogen-Doped Mesoporous Carbon Spheres with Ultrathin Nanosheets</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhong, Xiongwei; Li, Yingzhi; Zhang, Luozheng; Tang, Jun; Li, Xiangnan; Liu, Chang; Shao, Mengmeng; Lu, Zhouguang; Pan, Hui; Xu, Baomin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon exhibits high theor. capacity for sodium-ion batteries.  However, its practical application suffers from low elec. cond., poor electrochem. stability, and sluggish kinetics.  To tackle these challenges, novel nitrogen-doped carbon spheres with mesopores, ultrathin nanostructure, and optimal graphitization are prepd. by a three-step procedure.  It was found that the as-prepd. sample (NMCSs-800) with an optimal structure and nitrogen content delivers a high reversible sodium storage capacity of 334.7 mA h/g at 50 mA/g and an ultrahigh rate performance of 93.9 mA h/g at 5 A/g, which is better than most state-of-the-art carbon materials.  The improved energy storage capacity is attributed to its unique architecture and optimal nitrogen doping, which provide abundant active sites, defects, and voids.  Moreover, kinetic anal. and in situ Raman spectroscopy results reveal adsorption and adsorption-intercalation mechanisms for Na+ storage in hard carbon at the slope region above 0.3 V and the other slope region of 0.3-0.02 V, resp.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Heteroatom-doping is an effective way to regulate the electronic structure of carbon so as to improve their Na-ion storage capability.  In all kinds of heteroatoms, selenium (Se)-doping has rarely been investigated even though Se has unique physicochem. properties.  Herein, we report a facile fabrication of Se/N-codoped carbon nanosheets (N/Se-CNs) with 10 at% N and 2 at% Se by an oxidn.-selenization process.  The synchrotron XPS measurements indicate that Se doping can significantly change the electronic structures of carbon nanosheets, because Se can act as stronger electron-withdrawing units for Na storage compared with C and N.  Therefore, Se can better play the role of improving the cond. and wettability of the carbon materials.  And Se atoms effectively enlarge the interlayer distance of carbon nanosheets to enhance the Na-ion diffusion kinetics and also generate extra active sites for Na-ion storage.  Served as anode materials for SIBs, the N/Se-CNs delivers higher specific capacity and better rate capability compared with only N-doped carbon nanosheets.  Therefore, Se-doping is an effective way for improvement of Na-storage capability of carbon materials.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Kinetic study of the oxidation resistance of phosphorus-containing activated carbons</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Rosas, Juana Maria; Ruiz-Rosas, Ramiro; Rodriguez-Mirasol, Jose; Cordero, Tomas</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Chem. activation of different lignocellulosic materials with phosphoric acid produces activated carbons with higher oxidn. resistance than that obsd. for catalyst free chars obtained at similar conditions from the same biomass, even though the activated carbons have a more developed porous structure.  The main reason for such behavior is probably related to the presence of thermally stable phosphorus complexes that remain on the carbon surface after the activation process.  XPS analyses point out the oxidn. of the phosphorus reduced groups to C-O-PO3/(CO)2PO2 prior to carbon gasification.  The latter complexes seem to stabilize the active carbon sites.  Moreover, the presence of these phosphorus inhibitors produces a change in the gasification mechanism of the activated carbons with respect to that for char.  Char oxidn. seems to proceed in the entire available particle surface, while activated carbon gasification is better explained by the shrinking unreacted core model.  Such a difference in mechanism is attributed to the inhibition effect of the phosphorus complexes, which reduces the reactivity of carbon active sites, and could act as a phys. barrier for oxygen diffusion in the micropores.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqoXK6hG5KZRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj5WIyu0hOdag"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrahigh Phosphorus Doping of Carbon for High-Rate Sodium Ion Batteries Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Jie; Li, Haomiao; Wang, Kangli; Jin, Qianzheng; Lai, Chenglong; Wang, Ruxing; Cao, Shengling; Han, Jing; Zhang, Zhuchan; Su, Jinzhao; Jiang, Kai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phosphorus doped carbons are of particular interest as anode materials because of their large interlayer spacing and strong adsorption of Na+ ions.  However, it remains challenging to achieve high phosphorus doping due to the limited choices of phosphorus sources and the difficulty in constructing oxygen-free synthesis system.  Herein, a new synthesis strategy is proposed to prep. ultrahigh phosphorus-doped carbon (UPC) anodes for high performance sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  By using two commonly available, miscible, evaporable liqs. in PCl3 and C6H12, as phosphorus and carbon sources, an oxygen-free reaction system is successfully established by N2 bubbling to simultaneously realize carbonization and in situ P doping.  The P content can reach 30 wt%, much higher than most reported P-doping carbon-based materials.  Furthermore, the doped P is dominated by substitutional P-(C3) protrusions in the carbon lattice, which can significantly enlarge the interlayer spacing and enhance the adsorption energy of Na+.  When serving as the SIBs anode, the UPC delivers an ultrahigh reversible capacity of 510.4 mAh g-1 with a rational operating voltage of 0.54 V, and the best rate capability of 397.1 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1.  This new strategy will effectively promote the practical application of hard carbon.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp38e3qO8gFxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj5WIyu0hOdag"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXptFyrtbw%253D&amp;md5=8b1f8c120a246e87ea1133fb4e15d2ce</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b01349"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hasegawa, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deguchi, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kanamori, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kobayashi, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kageyama, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Abe, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nakanishi, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Level Doping of Nitrogen, Phosphorus, and Sulfur into Activated Carbon Monoliths and Their Electrochemical Capacitances</span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The present report demonstrates a new technique for doping heteroatoms (nitrogen, phosphorus, and sulfur) into carbon materials via a versatile post-treatment.  The heat-treatment of carbon materials with a reagent, which is stable at ambient temps. and evolves reactive gases on heating, in a vacuum-closed tube allows the introduction of various heteroatom-contg. functional groups into a carbon matrix.  In addn., the sequential doping reactions give rise to dual- and triple-heteroatom-doped carbons.  The pore properties of the precursor carbon materials are preserved through each heteroatom doping process, which indicates that independent tuning of heteroatom doping and nanostructural morphol. can be achieved in various carbon materials.  The electrochem. investigation on the undoped and doped carbon monolithic electrodes applied to supercapacitors provides insights into the effects of heteroatom doping on electrochem. capacitance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr9dtAGByPg_7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj5WIyu0hOdag"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Although tremendous efforts have been devoted to understanding the origin of boosted charge storage on heteroatom-doped carbons, none of the present studies has shown a whole landscape.  Herein, by both exptl. evidence and theor. simulation, it is demonstrated that heteroatom doping not only results in a broadened operating voltage, but also successfully promotes the specific capacitance in aq. supercapacitors.  In particular, the electrolyte cations adsorbed on heteroatom-doped carbon can effectively inhibit hydrogen evolution reaction, a key step of water decompn. during the charging process, which broadens the voltage window of aq. electrolytes even beyond the thermodn. limit of water (1.23 V).                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers derived from polyacrylonitrile for use as anode material in sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Jiadeng; Chen, Chen; Lu, Yao; Ge, Yeqian; Jiang, Han; Fu, Kun; Zhang, Xiangwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers (N-CNFs) derived from polyacrylonitrile were successfully synthesized by a combination of electrospinning and thermal treatment processes.  The as-prepd. N-CNFs were used as anode material for sodium-ion batteries due to their unique fabric and weakly-ordered turbostratic structure as well as large spacing between graphene layers.  Results show that N-CNFs carbonized at 800 °C delivered a high reversible capacity of 293 mAh/g at a c.d. of 50 mA/g in the first cycle.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Although sodium ion batteries (SIBs) possess many beneficial features, their rate performance, cycling stability, and safety need improvement for com. applications. The full utilization of fast bonding-debonding processes between the active sites and sodium ions could bring a capacitive strategy to achieve superior sodium storage properties.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High Capacity of Hard Carbon Anode in Na-Ion Batteries Unlocked by POx Doping</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zhifei; Ma, Lu; Surta, Todd Wesley; Bommier, Clement; Jian, Zelang; Xing, Zhenyu; Stickle, William F.; Dolgos, Michelle; Amine, Khalil; Lu, Jun; Wu, Tianpin; Ji, Xiulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The capacity of hard carbon anodes in Na-ion batteries rarely reaches values beyond 300 mAh/g.  It is reported that doping POx into local structures of hard carbon increases its reversible capacity from 283-359 mAh/g.  It is confirmed that the doped POx is redox inactive by X-ray adsorption near edge structure measurements, thus not contributing to the higher capacity.  Two significant changes are obsd. of hard carbon's local structures caused by doping.  First, the (002) d-spacing inside the turbostratic nanodomains is increased, revealed by both lab. and synchrotron X-ray diffraction.  Second, doping turns turbostratic nanodomains more defective along ab planes, indicated by neutron total scattering and the assocd. pair distribution function studies.  The local structural changes of hard carbon are correlated to the higher capacity, where both the plateau and slope regions in the potential profiles are enhanced.  The study demonstrates that Na-ion storage in hard carbon heavily depends on carbon local structures, where such structures, despite being disordered, can be tuned toward unusually high capacities.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqdu855Pkblf7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhsRKlPpFIs5w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtFOktLvL&amp;md5=1451c96d6ecdb7b2271ab49cd240507b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2020.156791"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jia, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sulfur and Phosphorus Co-doped Hard Carbon Derived from Oak Seeds Enabled Reversible Sodium Spheres Filling and Plating for Ultra-stable Sodium Storage</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sulfur and phosphorus co-doped hard carbon derived from oak seeds enabled reversible sodium spheres filling and plating for ultra-stable sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ding, Juan; Zhang, Yue; Huang, Yudai; Wang, Xingchao; Sun, Ying; Guo, Yong; Jia, Dianzeng; Tang, Xincun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">851</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">156791</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JALCEU</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon has been considered as a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries (SIBs), but suffers from poor rate performance and some safety issues caused by irreversible or undesirable sodium plating.  Heteroatom doping is an effective strategy to further improve the electrochem. performance of hard carbon.  Herein, biomass oak seeds are selected as carbon source to prep. S/P co-doped hard carbon through a simple one-step pyrolysis process.  The hard carbon pyrolyzed from oak seeds at 1000°C (C1000) exhibits excellent rate performance (initial discharge capacity is 136.1 mA h g-1) and remarkable cycling stability (1000 cycles with 88% capacity retention at 1000 mA g-1).  The unique S/P co-doping is very important to the high electrochem. performances, since sulfur and phosphorus co-doping enlarges interlayer distance, modifies the electronic structure, as well as provides more effective active sites, thereby enabling hard carbon with a fast, complete charge transfer kinetics of sodium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpPVWhhoBNC4LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhsRKlPpFIs5w"> &gt;&gt;
